"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The original price of each pack of DVDs is 76 dollars.\n2. There is a discount of 25 dollars on each pack.\n3. To find out how much you have to pay for each pack after the discount, subtract the discount from the original price.\n4. Therefore, the price you have to pay for each pack is 76 - 25.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 76 - 25 = 51.\n\nThe answer is 51 dollars."

Therefore, the total number of children on the bus after 82 got on is 28 + 82 = 110 children.\n4. After some children got off, there were 30 children left on the bus.\n5. To find out how many children got off the bus, we subtract the number of children remaining from the total number of children after 82 got on: 110 - 30 = 80 children got off.\n6. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Rachel learned that 703 visitors came to Buckingham Palace on the previous day.\n2. There were 246 visitors on the day they visited.\n3. The problem asks for the total number of visitors within 25 days.\n\nTo solve this, we need to make an assumption about the average number of visitors per day over the 25 days. Since we only have data for two specific days, we can calculate the average of these two days and assume it applies to the entire 25-day period.\n\n4. Calculate the average number of visitors for the two days:\n   - Day 1 (previous day): 703 visitors\n   - Day 2 (day they visited): 246 visitors\n   - Average visitors per day = (703 + 246) / 2 = 949 / 2 = 474.5\n\n5. Assume this average applies to all 25 days:\n   - Total visitors over 25 days = 474.5 visitors/day * 25 days = 11,862.5\n\nSince the number of visitors must be a whole number, we can round to the nearest whole number:\n\n6. Therefore, the estimated total number of visitors over 25 days is approximately 11,863.\n\nThe answer is 11,863."

To find out how many action figures Jerry added, we need to account for the deficit created by removing 10 figures and the final count of 8 figures.\n6. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Nell originally had 309 baseball cards.\n2. Nell originally had 356 Ace cards.\n3. The total number of cards Nell originally had is 309 + 356 = 665 cards.\n4. After giving some cards to Jeff, Nell has 415 cards left.\n5. To find out how many cards Nell gave to Jeff, we subtract the number of cards she has now from the original total: 665 - 415 = 250 cards.\n6. We need to determine how many more baseball cards than Ace cards Nell has now.\n7. Let \\( x \\) be the number of baseball cards Nell has now, and \\( y \\) be the number of Ace cards she has now.\n8. We know that \\( x + y = 415 \\).\n9. We also know that the difference between the original number of baseball and Ace cards is \\( 309 - 356 = -47 \\).\n10. Since Nell gave away 250 cards, the difference in the number of baseball and Ace cards she has now should be the same as the original difference, which is -47.\n11. Therefore, \\( x - y = -47 \\).\n12. We have two equations:\n    - \\( x + y = 415 \\)\n    - \\( x - y = -47 \\)\n13. Solving these equations simultaneously:\n    - Add the two equations: \\( (x + y) + (x - y) = 415 - 47 \\)\n    - This simplifies to \\( 2x = 368 \\)\n    - Solving for \\( x \\), we get \\( x = 184 \\).\n14. Substitute \\( x = 184 \\) back into the equation \\( x + y = 415 \\):\n    - \\( 184 + y = 415 \\)\n    - Solving for \\( y \\), we get \\( y = 231 \\).\n15. Therefore, Nell has 184 baseball cards and 231 Ace cards.\n16. The difference in the number of baseball cards and Ace cards is \\( 231 - 184 = 47 \\).\n\nThe answer is that Nell has 47 more Ace cards than baseball cards."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Initially, there were 36 children on the bus.\n2. 68 children got off the bus.\n3. After some children got on the bus, there were 12 children altogether on the bus.\n\nTo find out how many children got on the bus, we can set up the equation:\n\n- Initial number of children on the bus: 36\n- Number of children who got off the bus: 68\n- Number of children who got on the bus: \\( x \\)\n- Final number of children on the bus: 12\n\nThe equation is:\n\\[ 36 - 68 + x = 12 \\]\n\nSolving for \\( x \\):\n\\[ 36 - 68 + x = 12 \\]\n\\[ -32 + x = 12 \\]\n\\[ x = 12 + 32 \\]\n\\[ x = 44 \\]\n\nSo, 44 children got on the bus.\n\nNow, to find out how many more children got off the bus than those that got on, we subtract the number of children who got on from the number who got off:\n\n- Number of children who got off: 68\n- Number of children who got on: 44\n\nThe difference is:\n\\[ 68 - 44 = 24 \\]\n\nTherefore, 24 more children got off the bus than those that got on. The answer is 24."

Therefore, the total number of oranges harvested per day is 8 * 35.\n5. Performing the multiplication, we get 8 * 35 = 280.\n\nThe answer is 280 oranges per day."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Edward spent $16 to buy books.\n2. Edward spent $8 to buy pens.\n3. To find out how much more Edward spent on books than on pens, we subtract the amount spent on pens from the amount spent on books.\n4. Therefore, the difference in spending is $16 - $8.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get $16 - $8 = $8.\n\nThe answer is that Edward spent $8 more on books than on pens."

To find out how many minutes the machine worked, we divide the total number of shirts by the number of shirts it can make per minute.\n6. Therefore, the number of minutes the machine worked is 12 / 3.\n7. Performing the division, we get 12 / 3 = 4.\n\nThe answer is 4 minutes."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The number of red peaches in the basket is 19.\n2. The number of yellow peaches in the basket is 11.\n3. To find out how many more red peaches there are than yellow peaches, we subtract the number of yellow peaches from the number of red peaches.\n4. Therefore, the number of more red peaches than yellow peaches is 19 - 11.\n5. Performing the subtraction, we get 19 - 11 = 8.\n\nThe answer is 8. There are 8 more red peaches than yellow peaches in the basket."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Paul initially had 71 books.\n2. He bought 38 new books.\n3. After selling some books and buying new ones, he has a total of 116 books now.\n4. To find out how many books he sold, we need to determine the difference between the books he had after buying new ones and the books he has now.\n5. First, calculate the total number of books he would have if he hadn't sold any: 71 (initial) + 38 (bought) = 109 books.\n6. Since he has 116 books now, it means he sold some books and then bought more to reach 116.\n7. The difference between the books he would have had without selling and the books he has now is 116 - 109 = 7 books.\n8. This means he sold 7 books.\n9. To find out how many more books he bought than he sold, we compare the number of books bought to the number of books sold.\n10. He bought 38 books and sold 7 books.\n11. Therefore, he bought 38 - 7 = 31 more books than he sold.\n\nThe answer is 31."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. 41 campers went rowing in the morning.\n2. 4 campers went hiking in the morning.\n3. 26 campers went rowing in the afternoon.\n\nTo find the total number of unique campers who participated in either rowing or hiking throughout the day, we need to consider the possibility of overlap between the groups of campers who went rowing in the morning and those who went rowing in the afternoon. However, the problem does not provide information about whether the same campers participated in both morning and afternoon rowing sessions or if there was any overlap between rowing and hiking participants.\n\nAssuming no overlap between the morning and afternoon rowing sessions and no overlap between rowing and hiking participants, we can calculate the total number of unique campers as follows:\n\n- Total campers who went rowing (morning and afternoon combined) = 41 (morning) + 26 (afternoon) = 67 campers.\n- Total campers who went hiking = 4 campers.\n\nSince we are assuming no overlap, the total number of unique campers who participated in either rowing or hiking is the sum of the two groups:\n\n- Total unique campers = 67 (rowing) + 4 (hiking) = 71 campers.\n\nThe answer is 71 unique campers."

According to the information, Ed's current number of marbles is equal to Doug's current number of marbles plus 19. So, we have the equation:\n   \\[\n   x + 2 = (x - y) + 19\n   \\]\n6. Simplifying the equation:\n   \\[\n   x + 2 = x - y + 19\n   \\]\n7. Subtract \\( x \\) from both sides:\n   \\[\n   2 = -y + 19\n   \\]\n8. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. David did 38 push-ups.\n2. David did 56 more push-ups than Zachary.\n3. The correct approach is to set Zachary's push-ups as X, then David's push-ups = X + 56.\n9. Since David did 38 push-ups, we have X + 56 = 38.\n10. To find out how many bottle caps Danny had initially, we need to consider the changes in his collection:\n   - He threw away 60 bottle caps, which means he had 60 more bottle caps before throwing them away.\n   - He found 58 new bottle caps, which means he added 58 bottle caps to his collection.\n5. Let \\( x \\) be the initial number of bottle caps Danny had.\n6. After throwing away 60 bottle caps, he would have \\( x - 60 \\) bottle caps.\n7. Therefore, the number of more books than action figures is 10 - 6.\n7. Performing the subtraction, we get 10 - 6 = 4.\n\nThe answer is 4 more books than action figures."

Performing the multiplication, we get 67 * 66 = 4,422 students.\n6. Each school bus has 6 seats.\n7. To find the number of buses needed, we divide the total number of students by the number of seats on each bus.\n8. Number of buses needed = 4,422 / 6.\n9. Performing the division, we get 4,422 / 6 = 737 buses.\n\nThe answer is 737 buses are needed."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The Razorback t-shirt shop makes $87 off each t-shirt sold.\n2. They sold a total of 95 t-shirts during the Arkansas game and the Texas Tech game.\n3. To find out how many t-shirts were sold during the Texas Tech game, we subtract the number of t-shirts sold during the Arkansas game from the total number of t-shirts sold.\n4. They sold 47 t-shirts during the Arkansas game.\n5. Therefore, the number of t-shirts sold during the Texas Tech game is 95 - 47.\n6. Performing the subtraction, we get 95 - 47 = 48 t-shirts sold during the Texas Tech game.\n7. The total number of t-shirts sold is 95.\n8. To find out how much money they made from selling the t-shirts, we multiply the total number of t-shirts sold by the amount made per t-shirt.\n9. Therefore, the total money made is 95 * $87.\n10. Performing the multiplication, we get 95 * 87 = $8,265.\n\nThe answer is $8,265."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Initially, there are 3 birds sitting on the fence.\n2. An additional 2 birds join them.\n3. Therefore, the total number of birds on the fence is 3 + 2 = 5 birds.\n4. Additionally, 6 storks join the birds on the fence.\n5. Therefore, the total number of storks on the fence is 6 storks.\n6. To find out how many more storks than birds are sitting on the fence, we subtract the number of birds from the number of storks.\n7. Therefore, the difference is 6 storks - 5 birds = 1 more stork than birds.\n\nThe answer is 1 more stork than birds."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The waiter initially had 13 customers.\n2. Some customers left, and then he got 4 new customers.\n3. After these changes, he still had 9 customers remaining.\n\nTo find out how many customers left, we can set up the equation:\n\n- Initial customers - Customers who left + New customers = Remaining customers\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n- 13 - Customers who left + 4 = 9\n\nNow, solve for the number of customers who left:\n\n- 13 + 4 - Customers who left = 9\n- 17 - Customers who left = 9\n\nSubtract 9 from 17 to find the number of customers who left:\n\n- Customers who left = 17 - 9\n- Customers who left = 8\n\nThe answer is 8 customers left."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Jerry added 2 more action figures to the shelf.\n2. Jerry removed 7 of the old action figures from the shelf.\n3. There are currently 10 action figures on the shelf.\n\nTo find out how many action figures Jerry initially had, we need to consider the changes made to the initial number:\n\n4. Let \\( x \\) be the initial number of action figures on the shelf.\n5. After adding 2 action figures, the number becomes \\( x + 2 \\).\n6. Then, Jerry removed 7 action figures, so the number becomes \\( x + 2 - 7 \\).\n7. We know that after these changes, there are 10 action figures on the shelf.\n\nTherefore, we can set up the equation:\n\n\\[ x + 2 - 7 = 10 \\]\n\n8. Simplify the equation:\n\n\\[ x - 5 = 10 \\]\n\n9. Solve for \\( x \\) by adding 5 to both sides:\n\n\\[ x = 10 + 5 \\]\n\n10. Therefore, \\( x = 15 \\).\n\nThe answer is that Jerry initially had 15 action figures on the shelf."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Rachel picked 7 apples from the tree.\n2. After Rachel picked the apples, 2 new apples grew on the tree.\n3. The tree currently has 6 apples on it.\n\nTo find out how many apples the tree had initially, we need to consider the apples that were picked and the new ones that grew:\n\n4. First, calculate the total number of apples that were on the tree after Rachel picked 7 apples and before the 2 new apples grew. Since there are currently 6 apples on the tree, and 2 new ones grew, the number of apples before the new ones grew is 6 - 2 = 4 apples.\n\n5. Since Rachel picked 7 apples, the initial number of apples on the tree was the 4 apples (before the new ones grew) plus the 7 apples that were picked.\n\n6. Therefore, the initial number of apples on the tree was 4 + 7 = 11 apples.\n\nThe answer is 11."

Therefore, the number of people on the bus after 12 more got on is 8 + 12 = 20.\n5. Then, 3 people got off the bus.\n6. Therefore, the number of people on the bus now is 20 - 3 = 17.\n\nThe answer is 17."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Initially, the waiter had 3 customers.\n2. After some customers left, the waiter had 4 customers remaining.\n3. This means that new customers must have arrived because the number of customers increased from 3 to 4.\n4. The number of customers who stayed behind is 4.\n5. The number of customers who left is calculated by considering the initial number of customers and the new arrivals. Since the number of customers increased, we need to determine how many new customers arrived.\n6. Let's assume \\( x \\) new customers arrived. Then, the equation is: \n   \\[\n   3 - (\\text{number of customers who left}) + x = 4\n   \\]\n7. Solving for \\( x \\), we find that \\( x = 1 \\) (since 3 + 1 = 4).\n8. Therefore, the number of customers who left is \\( 3 - 1 = 2 \\).\n9. To find how many more customers stayed behind than those that left, calculate the difference between the number of customers who stayed (4) and the number who left (2).\n10. Therefore, the difference is \\( 4 - 2 = 2 \\).\n\nThe answer is 2."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Adam has 4 more apples than Jackie.\n2. Together, Adam and Jackie have 14 apples.\n3. Let the number of apples Jackie has be \\( x \\).\n4. Then, the number of apples Adam has is \\( x + 4 \\).\n5. Together, Adam and Jackie have \\( x + (x + 4) = 14 \\) apples.\n6. Simplifying the equation: \\( 2x + 4 = 14 \\).\n7. Subtract 4 from both sides: \\( 2x = 10 \\).\n8. Divide both sides by 2: \\( x = 5 \\).\n9. So, Jackie has 5 apples, and Adam has \\( 5 + 4 = 9 \\) apples.\n10. Together, Adam and Jackie have 14 apples, which matches the given information.\n11. Bob has 6 apples more than Adam and Jackie together.\n12. Therefore, Bob has \\( 14 + 6 = 20 \\) apples.\n\nThe answer is 20."

Therefore, the number of cards Nell gave to Jeff is 528 - 252.\n6. Performing the subtraction, we get 528 - 252 = 276.\n\nThe answer is Nell gave 276 cards to Jeff."

Therefore, the number of students going on the trip is 102 - 22 = 80.\n4. Each school bus has 8 seats.\n5. To find out how many buses are needed, we need to divide the total number of students going on the trip by the number of seats on each bus.\n6. Therefore, the number of buses needed is 80 divided by 8.\n7. Performing the division, we get 80 / 8 = 10.\n\nThe answer is 10 buses are needed."

Therefore, the total number of chairs is 10 * 6 = 60 chairs.\n5. There are 11 people sitting on chairs.\n6. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We have information about the number of visitors for three specific days:\n   - On the current day, there were 512 visitors.\n   - On the previous day, there were 471 visitors.\n   - Two days before the current day, there were 808 visitors.\n\n2. We need to estimate the number of visitors over the past 89 days. However, we only have data for three specific days, and no information is provided about the other 86 days.\n\n3. Without additional information or an average number of visitors per day, we cannot accurately calculate the total number of visitors over the past 89 days.\n\n4. If we assume that the number of visitors on the other 86 days is similar to the average of the three given days, we can calculate an estimate. However, this assumption may not be accurate without further data.\n\n5. To find the average number of visitors for the three given days:\n   - Total visitors for the three days = 512 + 471 + 808 = 1,791 visitors.\n   - Average visitors per day for these three days = 1,791 / 3 = 597 visitors (approximately).\n\n6. If we assume this average holds for the entire 89-day period, we can estimate the total number of visitors:\n   - Estimated total visitors over 89 days = 597 * 89 = 53,133 visitors.\n\n7. This is a rough estimate based on the assumption that the average number of visitors per day is consistent with the three days for which we have data.\n\nThe estimated number of visitors over the past 89 days is approximately 53,133, assuming the average number of visitors per day is similar to the three given days."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The area of the carpet needed to cover the room is 10 square feet.\n2. The length of the room is given as 5 feet.\n3. The area of a rectangle (which is the shape of the room) is calculated by multiplying its length by its width.\n4. Therefore, the area of the room is given by the formula: Area = Length  Width.\n5. We know the area is 10 square feet and the length is 5 feet, so we can set up the equation: 10 = 5  Width.\n6. To find the width, we need to divide the area by the length: Width = 10 / 5.\n7. Performing the division, we get Width = 2 feet.\n\nThe answer is that the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet."
